<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<section class="tab-pane pure-u-1-1 u-printing-display-inline-ie u-printing-display-inline-ff">
		<!-- ngIf: vm.loading -->
		<!-- ngIf: !vm.loading --><div ng-if="!vm.loading" class="ng-scope">
			<!-- uiView: --><div ui-view="" class="ng-scope"><section class="pure-u-1-1 document-abstract document-tab u-p-2 ng-isolate-scope" mathjax-bind="" id="6949620">

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1' : 'pure-u-1-1'" class="ng-scope pure-u-1-1">
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement -->
		<!--/div-->
		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this letter, we investigate the impact of washing on the performance of passive ultra-high frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) tags based on dipole antennas fabricated from silver and copper fabrics. Initially, the tags achieved read ranges of 6 and 10.8 m, respectively, under the European RFID emission regulation. To assess the impact of washing on the performance of the tags, they were washed repeatedly in a washing machine and measured after every washing cycle. The silver fabric tag was found to be more durable without any coating and maintained a read range of over 2 m after 10 washing cycles. We also tested two conformal coatings to protect the tags from wear and tear during washing and found regular textile glue to be a promising conformal coating for both types of textile tags. Finally, we present simulation results to confirm the relationship between reduction in the antenna conductivity and the measured read ranges of the tags during the washing test.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Recently, many innovative applications of wearable electronics have appeared, and the future expectations on the technology are high. For example, wearable radio-frequency identification (RFID) tags have an enormous potential in future welfare and healthcare applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Textile conductors created for instance by printing of inks with metallic inclusions, embroidery with metal-coated sewing thread, and patterning of metallized fabrics are examples of technologies that have a great potential in this research endeavor. These methods and materials have been used to create lightweight and conformal transmission lines, waveguides, and antennas for wireless body area networks <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. In addition to being conformal, lightweight, and comfortable to wear, a wearable antenna needs to withstand various environmental conditions, such as crumpling <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, stretching <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, and washing <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>.</p><p>In this letter, antennas for wearable passive ultra-high frequency (UHF) RFID tags were fabricated from commercially available silver and copper fabrics. In addition, two different conformal coatings were tested. To evaluate the reliability of the tags, they were washed repeatedly in a household washing machine using a common 40 °C washing program with detergent and spinning and tested wirelessly after each washing cycle. All the tags were washed at the same time in a single washing bag with no other laundry. The impact of reduction in the antenna conductivity on the performance of the tags was also studied through simulations.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Studied antenna structure.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Design and Fabrication of the Textile Tags</h2></div><p>We chose the antennas to be T-matched dipoles with the structure shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. This a very common class of antennas used in UHF RFID tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>. In this work, the length (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">L</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the antenna was chosen to be 100 mm, which is similar to many commercial products and sufficient to avoid the ailments of electrically small antennas in the considered frequencies from 800 MHz to 1 GHz. Referring to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, the major design goal was to optimize the parameters <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-7" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">b</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to achieve an inductive antenna input impedance for complex conjugate impedance matching with a capacitive tag. The antenna design is described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a>, where the silver fabric tag was developed for a stretching durability test. The tag was optimized for operation at 940 MHz because a downward frequency shift due to antenna elongation was anticipated.</p><p>The tag IC we used was NXP UCODE G2iL series RFID IC with the wake-up power of −18 dBm (15.8<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.87em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">~\mu\hbox{W}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). The chip was attached by the manufacturer in a fixture patterned from copper on a plastic film. We attached the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-17" role="math" style="width: 5.228em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.688em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1004.69em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">3</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.99em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.985em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">3\times 3\hbox{-mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> pads of the fixture to the textile antenna using conductive epoxy. After curing of the electrical antenna–IC joint, we shielded the IC and the textile around with regular textile glue in order to protect the antenna–IC joint from the mechanical stress and dissolution of conductive particles during washing.</p><p>The prototype tags were patterned from Less EMF Stretch Conductive Fabric (Cat. #321) and Less EMF Pure Copper Polyester Taffeta Fabric (Cat. #A1212). Both fabrics are thin and lightweight, and they can be easily cut with scissors. Finally, regular textile glue (Gutermann Creativ HT2) and PALC textile moisture protection spray were applied to completely cover sample tags. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the microscope images of the coated and noncoated fabric surfaces.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Microscope images (magnification 5×) of (A) silver fabric without coating, (B) silver fabric with glue coating, (C) silver fabric with PALC coating, (D) copper fabric without coating, (E) copper fabric with glue coating, and (F) copper fabric with PALC coating.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results and Discussion</h2></div><p>The performance of the fabricated textile RFID tags was analyzed based on the measured threshold power. It is the minimum output power of an RFID reader to activate the tag under test from a given distance. In free space, the threshold power can be expressed as <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-29" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 27.511em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 111%; min-width: 27.511em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.345em 1023.37em 6.189em -999.997em); top: -4.502em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="min-width: 27.511em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; margin-left: -11.709em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.345em 1023.37em 6.189em -999.997em); top: -4.502em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 23.366em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.826em 1023.37em 6.67em -999.997em); top: -4.982em; left: 50%; margin-left: -11.709em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-41"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-44"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-47"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-48"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-49" style="font-size: 70.7%; Threshold power can be measured using a reader with adjustable output power or with RFID testers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a>. width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.607em 1004.81em 3.967em -999.997em); top: -5.462em; left: 1.024em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.808em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; font-family: MathJax_Main; top: -4.021em; left: -0.057em;">−<span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.958em 1001.2em 0.423em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.2em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.081em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(2)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-337"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-338"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-339"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-340"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-341"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-343"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(2)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -1.463em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 3.47em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-17">{d_{\rm Tag}} = {\lambda \over {4\pi}}\sqrt {{{{\rm EIRP} {P_{\rm TS{\ast}}}} \over {{\rm \Lambda }{P_{\rm TS}}}}} \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{d_{\rm Tag}} = {\lambda \over {4\pi}}\sqrt {{{{\rm EIRP} {P_{\rm TS{\ast}}}} \over {{\rm \Lambda }{P_{\rm TS}}}}} \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-402" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-403"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Λ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">\Lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a known parameter (unit: watts) describing the sensitivity of the measurement system reference tag and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-405" role="math" style="width: 2.225em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.99em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-406"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-407"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-408" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-409"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-410"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-411" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-412" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-414"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-415" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">∗</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">P_{\rm TS{\ast}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the measured threshold power of the reference tag. In this letter, we report all the read-range results under the European RFID emission regulation: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-416" role="math" style="width: 7.691em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.91em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1006.91em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-417"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-418"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-419"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-420" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">E</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-421" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-422" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-423" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">P</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-424" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-425" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">3.28</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-426" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-427"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-428"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-429" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">{\rm EIRP }= 3.28~\hbox{W}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the direction of the positive <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-430" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-431"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-432" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. In all measurements, the dipole tag was aligned for polarization matching with a linearly polarized reader antenna.</p><p>The attainable read range based on threshold power measurement for noncoated, glue-coated, and PALC-coated silver fabric tags can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 3</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link"></a> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a>, respectively. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 6</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link"></a> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">8</a> show the attainable read range of noncoated, glue-coated, and PALC-coated copper fabric tags, respectively. Here, the result “adding glue” shows the impact of shielding the tag IC with the textile glue. After this, the tags were washed up to 10 times or until the read range had reduced below 1 m, which was considered as a failure limit in our experiment.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Measurement result for noncoated silver tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Measurement result of glue-coated silver tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The results presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> show that, initially, the noncoated silver fabric tag achieved the attainable read range close to 6 m at the design frequency of 940 MHz. Shielding the IC with the textile glue reduced this by approximately 30 cm, which is explained by the minor impact of the glue on antenna impedance. After this, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-433" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-434"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-435"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-436"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-437"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-438" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-439"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-440"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-441" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-442" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-443" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">{d_{\rm tag}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reduced at all frequency and after each wash repetitions <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-444" role="math" style="width: 5.889em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.288em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.29em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-445"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-446"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-447"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-448"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-449" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-450"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-451"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-452" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-453" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-454" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-455" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≈</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-456" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.7</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-457" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-458"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-459"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-460" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">{d_{\rm tag}} \approx 2.7~\hbox{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 940 MHz, which is sufficient in many applications. Comparison of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 3</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link"></a> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a> reveals first that prior coating the performance of the studied tag samples is nearly identical, which enables the fair comparison of their performance after washing and coating. Moreover, the glue coating had a negligible impact on the performance of the tag (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>), whereas PALC coating reduced <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-461" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-462"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-463"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-464"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-465"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-466" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-467"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-468"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-469" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-470" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-471" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">{d_{\rm tag}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by approximately 1.5 m.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Measurement result of PALC-coated silver tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 4</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a>, washing had a detrimental impact also on glue- and PALC-coated silver fabric tags. However, the glue-coated tags maintained the read range of 4 m after 10 washing cycles (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>), and after seven wash repetitions, there was little change in the read range. Thus, the coating with regular textile glue was clearly seen to help the textile tags to endure washing. On the other hand, the tested textile moisture protection spray coating was found to have almost no effect on the performance of the silver fabric tags: The PALC-coated tags performed very similarly to the noncoated tags and were readable from the distances of 2–2.5 m after 10 washing cycles (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>).</p><p>The copper fabric tags initially achieved the attainable read range close to 11 m at the frequency of 950 MHz. Similar to the silver fabric tags, the shielding of the IC with the textile glue had a minor negative impact on the tag performance: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-472" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-473"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-475"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-476"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-477" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-478"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-479"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-480" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-481" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-482" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">{d_{\rm tag}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reduced to 9.8 m at 935 MHz. This is still notably higher than for the silver fabric tags due to the higher conductivity of the copper fabric. However, as seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, despite the high initial performance, after three washing cycles, the read range of the noncoated copper fabric tags had dropped to 2.5 m, and after the fourth wash repetition, they became dysfunction. Thus, the conformal coating is needed to make these tags washable.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Measurement result for noncoated copper tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Comparison of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 6</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link"></a> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">8</a> shows that prior coating the performance of the studied tag samples was nearly identical, enabling the fair comparison of their performance after washing and coating. As in the case of the silver fabric tags, the glue coating was found to provide better protection also the copper fabric tags: After 10 washing cycles, the glue-coated copper fabric tags maintained the read ranges of almost 5 m (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>). The tested textile moisture protection spray coating was found not to improve the reliability of the copper fabric tags: They became dysfunctional after four washing cycles (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Measurement result of glue-coated copper tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Measurement result of PALC-coated copper tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As seen from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a>, two antenna parameters susceptible to the detrimental impact of washing are the tag antenna gain (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-483" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.2em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-484"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-485"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-486"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-487"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-488" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-489"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-490"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-491" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">{G_{\rm a}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and the antenna–IC power transfer efficiency (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-492" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-493"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-494" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">τ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.603em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">\tau</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). Since the tag IC was well shielded with the textile glue and its temperature rating of 85 °C is well beyond the washing temperature of 40 °C, we expect that the chip impedance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-495" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-496"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-497"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-499"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-500" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-502"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">{Z_{\rm ic}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and wake-up power (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-505" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-506"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-507"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-508"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-509"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-510" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-512"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-513" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-514" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-515" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">{P_{\rm ic0}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) were not significantly affected by the washing. Moreover, since we did not observe any change in the antenna shape and size, it was concluded that the tag antenna directivity (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-516" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-518"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-519"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-520"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-521" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-522"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-523"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-524" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">{D_{\rm a}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) was not affected by the washing. Hence, performance reduction due to washing was attributed to the dissolution of the conductive material from the textile, which is expected to reduce the antenna radiation efficiency (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-525" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.84em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-526"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-527"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-530" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-531"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-532"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-533" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">{e_{\rm r}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and influenced the antenna impedance. Here, we note that the antenna gain is linked to radiation efficiency and directivity through: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-534" role="math" style="width: 5.228em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.688em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.69em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-535"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-536"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-537"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-538"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-539" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-540"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-541"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-542" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-543" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-544" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-545"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-546"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-547" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-548"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-549"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-550" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-553"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-554" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-556"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{G_{\rm a}} = {e_{\rm r}}{D_{\rm a}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>To investigate the impact of reduction in the antenna conductivity further, we simulated the antenna using ANSYS HFSS ver. 15 with various sheet resistance values assigned for the conductor, which was modeled as an impedance boundary. The measured values of 1.25 and 0.4<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-558" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-559"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-560" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-561" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>/sq were used as the sheet resistance of the silver and copper fabric tags, respectively, in their initial condition <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3">[13]</a>. Based on <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3">[14]</a>, the tag IC was modeled as a parallel connection of a resistance of 2.85 k <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-562" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-564" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and capacitance of 0.91 pF resulting in an impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-565" role="math" style="width: 5.408em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.868em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.81em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-566"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-567" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">12</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-568" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-569" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-570" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">185</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-571" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">12-j185 \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 940 MHz.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Simulation of the noncoated silver fabric tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Simulation of the noncoated copper fabric tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/6949620/6949620-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Simulated attainable read ranges of the (top) noncoated silver and (bottom) copper fabric tags for various values of the sheet resistance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6949620/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The simulation results are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 9</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link"></a> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">11</a>. Overall, they show that the increase in the sheet resistance of the antenna not only reduces the radiation efficiency of the antenna, but also notably detunes it (reduces <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-572" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-573"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-574" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">τ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.603em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">\tau</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) through an increase in the antenna resistance. In practice, this may have been caused by several factors, including wear and tear leading to microcracks and dissolution of the conductive material leading nonuniform and thinned conductor with increased current crowding. Furthermore, comparison of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 3</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">11</a> shows that for the silver fabric tag, 9×increase in the sheet resistance value (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-575" role="math" style="width: 6.129em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.529em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.47em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-576"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-577"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-578"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-581"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-582"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-583" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-584" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-585" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">11.25</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-586" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">{R_{\rm s}} = 11.25\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>/sq) matches well with the measured results after 10 wash repetitions. Similarly, comparison of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 6</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">11</a> suggests that after three wash repetitions, the sheet resistance of the copper fabric had increased to more than 9×from the initial value. However, the temporary downward frequency-shift seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link"></a> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">8</a> was not predicted by the simulation and was not present for the silver fabric tag. This may have been due to a strongly localized or nonuniform distribution of stress during the washings test.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>Textile antennas enable seamlessly integrated wearable RFID tags and other wireless devices in body area networks. We studied the impact of washing on silver and copper fabric textile UHF RFID tags. Tag samples were washed in a household washing machine in a 40 °C washing program with detergent and spinning and tested wirelessly after each washing. The silver fabric tag was found to be washable more than 10 times without coating, but the noncoated copper fabric tag became dysfunctional after four wash repetitions. Furthermore, we found regular textile glue to be a fit conformal coating for both silver and copper fabric tags: The glue-coated tags maintained read ranges of 4 and 5 m after 10 wash repetitions, respectively. Simulations with reduced antenna conductivity corroborated that this was the main source of the tag performance reduction in the washing test.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

Study on the Washing Durability of Electro-Textile UHF RFID Tags","abstract":"In this letter, we investigate the impact of washing on the performance of passive ultra-high frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) tags based on dipole antennas fabricated from silver and copper fabrics. Initially, the tags achieved read ranges of 6 and 10.8 m, respectively, under the European RFID emission regulation. To assess the impact of washing on the performance of the tags, they were washed repeatedly in a washing machine and measured after every washing cycle. The silver fabric tag was found to be more durable without any coating and maintained a read range of over 2 m after 10 washing cycles. We also tested two conformal coatings to protect the tags from wear and tear during washing and found regular textile glue to be a promising conformal coating for both types of textile tags. Finally, we present simulation results to confirm the relationship between reduction in the antenna conductivity and the measured read ranges of the tags during the washing test.","rightsLink":"http://s100.copyright.com/AppDispatchServlet?publisherName=ieee&amp;publication=1536-1225&amp;title=Experimental+Study+on+the+Washing+Durability+of+Electro-Textile+UHF+RFID+Tags&amp;isbn=&amp;publicationDate=2015&amp;author=Yan+Yan+Fu&amp;ContentID=10.1109/LAWP.2014.2368212&amp;orderBeanReset=true&amp;startPage=466&amp;endPage=469&amp;volumeNum=14","displayPublicationTitle":"IEEE Antennas and Wireless Propagation Letters","pdfPath":"/iel7/7727/7024204/06949620.pdf","isJournal":true,"isConference":false,"dateOfInsertion":"05 February 2015","publicationDate":"2015","conferenceDate":" ","isACM":false,"volume":"14","isFreeDocument":false,"isPromo":false,"journalDisplayDateOfPublication":"07 November 2014","chronOrPublicationDate":"2015","isDynamicHtml":true,"isSMPTE":false,"isCustomDenial":false,"persistentLink":"http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/servlet/opac?punumber=7727","isStaticHtml":true,"isNotDynamicOrStatic":false,"htmlAbstractLink":"/document/6949620/","isStandard":false,"publisher":"IEEE","isEphemera":false,"isOpenAccess":false,"isEarlyAccess":false,"isBook":false,"accessionNumber":"14907302","htmlLink":"/document/6949620/","startPage":"466","fundingAgencies":{"fundingAgency":[{"fundingId":"10.13039/501100000780","fundingName":"European Commission Marie Curie"},{"fundingId":"","fundingName":"Finnish Funding Agency for Technology and Innovation"}]},"openAccessFlag":"no","ephemeraFlag":"false","title":"Experimental Study on the Washing Durability of Electro-Textile UHF RFID Tags","confLoc":"","accessionNumber":"14907302","ml_html_flag":"true","html_flag":"true","content_type":"Journals &amp;
